Lunding v. Tax Appeals Tribunal


74021


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


218 A.D.2d 268; 639 N.Y.S.2d 519; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2277



March 14, 1996, Decided  
March 14, 1996, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended April 22, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer appealed a determination from respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal of the State of New York, which disallowed the taxpayer's alimony deduction because he was a not a resident of New York. The taxpayer alleged that N.Y. Tax Law § 631(b)(6) violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer derived substantial income in New York during 1990. As a Connecticut resident, he timely filed a nonresident New York State personal income tax return and included alimony paid to his former spouse, also a Connecticut resident. The taxpayer sought a deduction for a portion of the alimony paid. The Audit Division of the Department of Taxation and Finance (division) disallowed the deduction and issued a notice of deficiency. The taxpayer contended that N.Y. Tax Law § 631(b)(6) was unconstitutional. An Administrative Law Judge found that neither the division nor the Tax Appeals Tribunal had jurisdiction to determine whether a statute was unconstitutional and upheld the disallowance of the deduction. On appeal, the court annulled the determination of the Tax Appeals Tribunal and held that the statute was unconstitutional. The denial of the alimony deduction to nonresidents violated the privilege and immunity clause. Because federal policy regarding the alimony deduction recognized that tax consequences fell upon the recipients of the alimony, not the payors, there existed no substantial reason for the disparate treatment of resident and nonresident alimony payors.


OUTCOME: The court declared the statute that treated resident and nonresident alimony payers differently was unconstitutional and annulled the determination of the Tax Appeals Tribunal that denied the taxpayer the alimony deduction.


HEADNOTES

Actions - Improper Form of Action - Challenge to Constitutionality of Statute In a proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 to review a determination of respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal which sustained a personal income tax assessment, that portion of the proceeding which seeks a declaration that Tax Law § 631 (b) (6) is unconstitutional is converted into a declaratory judgment action, as a proceeding commenced pursuant to CPLR article 78 is not the proper vehicle to challenge the constitutionality of a statute.

Taxation - Personal Income Tax - Alimony Deduction for Nonresident Taxpayer A determination which sustained a personal income tax assessment against petitioner, a resident of Connecticut who derived substantial income in New York, and who deducted the percentage of alimony paid to his former spouse, also a Connecticut resident, which represented the amount of business income derived from or connected with this State, is annulled, and Tax Law § 631 (b) (6), which provides that nonresident taxpayers may not take the alimony deduction authorized by the Internal Revenue Code (see, 26 USC § 215), is declared unconstitutional as violative of the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the US Constitution (US Const, art IV, § 2). After the Appellate Division held Tax Law former § 632 violative of the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the US Constitution (US Const, art IV, § 2) by denying the nonresident petitioner, employed in New York and living in Connecticut, the income tax adjustment for alimony paid to his nonresident ex-spouse ( Matter of Friedsam v State Tax Commn., 98 AD2d 26, affd 64 NY2d 76), the Court of Appeals affirmed on statutory grounds, and the Legislature enacted Tax Law § 631 (b) (6), which provides express statutory authority to deny the alimony deduction to nonresidents. The addition of Tax Law § 631 (b) (6) does not alter or undermine the Appellate Division's previous findings concerning the constitutionality of such practice or present a compelling reason to reach a different result on the identical legal issue. The legislative history behind Tax Law § 631 (b) (6) reveals no stated reason or discussion addressing the rationale underlying a denial to only nonresidents of the alimony deduction authorized by the Internal Revenue Code in proportion with their New York income. Since Federal policy regarding the alimony deduction recognizes that tax consequences should fall upon the recipients of the alimony, not the payors, and that denial of the deduction to a nonresident taxpayer ignores where the recipient resides or whether the recipient is taxed by this State, there is no substantial reason for the disparate treatment, leaving as the only criterion whether the payor is a resident or nonresident, and without more, there results a constitutional violation.

People v. Montes


0111


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


225 A.D.2d 1052; 639 N.Y.S.2d 610; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2883



March 8, 1996, Decided  
March 8, 1996, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions in the Supreme Court, Monroe County (New York), for depraved indifference murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with two counts of murder in the second degree, intentional murder and depraved indifference murder, after they beat the victim to death following a bar fight. They were acquitted of intentional murder and convicted of depraved indifference murder. On appeal, one defendant argued that the evidence of depravity was insufficient to support the conviction, both defendants argued that their convictions were against the weight of the evidence, and one defendant sought modification of his sentence. The court held that the argument concerning the evidence of depravity was not preserved for review where defendant did not articulate the specific ground in his motion to dismiss at the close of the People's case. The court further held that the convictions were not against the weight of the evidence, concluding that a finding that defendants had not acted with depraved indifference to human life would have been unreasonable. Finally, the court declined to exercise its power to modify one defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments convicting defendants of depraved indifference murder.

 

302 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Capital Fin. Corp. v. Commissioner of Taxation & Fin.


73638


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


218 A.D.2d 230; 639 N.Y.S.2d 501; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2042



March 7, 1996, Decided  
March 7, 1996, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mortgage corporation sought review of a determination of respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal (New York), which, inter alia, denied the corporation's application for a refund of unused special additional mortgage recording tax credit and interest due under N.Y. Tax Law art. 9-A.


OVERVIEW: The corporation incurred liability for payment of special additional mortgage recording taxes. N.Y. Tax Law § 253(1-a)(a). Under N.Y. Tax Law § 210 (17) (a), taxpayers were allowed a credit against the corporation franchise tax imposed by N.Y. Tax Law art. 9-A for the amount of special additional mortgage recording tax paid. Previously, any unused portion of the credit could be carried over to the following year and applied against the franchise tax for that year. N.Y. Tax Law § 210 (17)(b). An amendment to § 210 (17) (b), added the proviso that a credit attributable to special additional mortgage recording tax that was due and paid in any taxable year beginning before January 1, 1986 could not be carried over. The corporation challenged a determination of the lower court that by operation of the amendment it lost the benefit of an unused credit. On appeal the court conceded that the amendment had a negative effect on the corporation. However, the court held that the corporation failed to satisfy its heavy burden of demonstrating the unconstitutionality of amendment. The court also rejected the corporation's equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination of the lower court. The court dismissed the corporation's petition to annul the determination of the lower court and declared that the tax law had not been shown to be unconstitutional on its face or as applied to the corporation.


HEADNOTES

Actions - Conversion of One Form of Action to Another - Constitutionality of Tax Statute A CPLR article 78 proceeding challenging, on constitutional grounds, the determination of respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal, which, inter alia, denied petitioner's application for a refund of unused special mortgage recording tax credit and interest due under Tax Law article 9-A for the year 1985, is converted to a combined proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 and action for declaratory judgment since, although appropriate for the branch of the petition seeking annulment of the Tribunal's determination, a CPLR article 78 proceeding is not the proper vehicle for challenging the constitutionality of a statute.

Taxation - Franchise Tax on Business Corporations - Refund of Unused Special Mortgage Recording Tax Credit - Due Process The 1986 amendment to Tax Law § 210 (17) (former [b]), which provided, inter alia, that the credit against the corporation franchise tax attributable to special additional mortgage recording tax that was due and paid in any taxable year beginning before January 1, 1986 shall not be carried over to taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 1986, is not violative of due process merely because the amendment had the negative effect of depriving petitioner of an unused credit in the amount of $ 119,906 that had accumulated as of the close of 1985 in connection with its business of obtaining mortgages, since petitioner had no vested property right in the special additional mortgage recording tax credits it had earned, but did not use, prior to January 1, 1986. Petitioner has no vested entitlement to a continuation of the legislative favor of permitting excess credits to be applied against future tax liabilities. The Legislature has very nearly unconstrained authority in the design of taxing impositions.

Taxation - Franchise Tax on Business Corporations - Refund of Unused Special Mortgage Recording Tax Credit - Equal Protection The 1986 amendment to Tax Law § 210 (17) (former [b]), which provided, inter alia, that the credit against the corporation franchise tax attributable to special additional mortgage recording tax that was due and paid in any taxable year beginning before January 1, 1986 shall not be carried over to taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 1986, thereby having the negative effect of depriving petitioner of an unused credit in the amount of $ 119,906 that had accumulated as of the close of 1985 in connection with its business of obtaining mortgages, is not violative of equal protection since neither the exercise of a fundamental right nor a suspect classification is at issue, and the challenged classification is rationally related to achievement of a legitimate State purpose. Although the statute's negative impact is limited to those corporate taxpayers carrying excess credits at the close of 1985, neither the Federal nor State Constitution requires that all taxpayers be treated identically, only that those similarly situated be treated uniformly. Accordingly, even accepting the claim that the amendment can be viewed as "singling out 1985 filers", petitioner failed to establish legislative action that distinguished between taxpayers in a fashion that was "palpably arbitrary" or tantamount to "invidious discrimination".

 

303 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Straniere v. Silver


74286


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


218 A.D.2d 80; 637 N.Y.S.2d 982; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1301



February 22, 1996, Decided  
February 22, 1996, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 6, 1996.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which, inter alia, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. CPLR art. 78, granted respondent legislators' motion to dismiss the petition for failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: In an action involving the proposed secession of the Borough of Staten Island from the City of New York (City), appellants sought to annul the legislators' determination that a home rule message from the City was required before the secession bill could be reported out of the Committee. The legislators sought summary judgment on the basis that the proceeding was barred by the Speech or Debate Clause, N.Y. Const. art III, § 11, or, alternatively, that petitioners' claims were not justiciable. The supreme court granted the motion and dismissed the petition with prejudice, as absolutely barred by the Speech or Debate Clause. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court agreed with the supreme court that the Speaker's decision to require a home rule message for the Secession Bill was an integral part of the legislative process, and thus a legislative act for which the legislators were immune by virtue of the Speech or Debate Clause. The court held that once a determination is made that the action is within the purview of legitimate legislative activity, the court's review must end.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the supreme court granting the legislators' motion to dismiss the petition.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law - Speech or Debate Clause - Immunity of Legislators for Legislative Activities - Determination of Assembly Speaker to Require Home Rule Message for Secession Legislation for Borough of Staten Island A proceeding challenging the determination of respondents, the Speaker of the New York State Assembly and the Assembly's home rule counsel, that proposed legislation providing for the secession of the Borough of Staten Island from the City of New York requires a home rule message from the City (NY Const, art IX, § 2 [b] [2]) before the bill can be reported out of the Assembly's Cities Committee, is barred by the Speech or Debate Clause of the State Constitution (NY Const, art III, § 11), which shields legislators or their aides from litigation for any acts within the performance of their legislative function. The Speaker's decision to require a home rule message for the secession legislation was an integral part of the legislative process, and thus a "legislative act" for which respondents are immune by virtue of the Speech or Debate Clause. There is no merit to petitioners' arguments that Speech or Debate Clause immunity begins with the onset of committee deliberations or that the Speech or Debate Clause does not shield erroneous determinations by legislators or their staffs. Judicial review must be limited to determining whether the challenged action constitutes a legitimate legislative activity. Once a determination is made that the action is within the purview of legitimate legislative activity, the court's review must end.

308 of 992 DOCUMENTS


MATTER OF MATHIS v WETZLER


73718


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


217 A.D.2d 151; 635 N.Y.S.2d 809; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 33



January 4, 1996, Decided  
January 4, 1996, Entered



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, on the law, without costs, determination confirmed and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner executor sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which reversed a decision of respondent Department of Taxation and Finance, which denied the executor's request for a refund of estate taxes under N.Y. Tax. Law § 249-aa. The executor contended that she was entitled to interest from the date the Department received the tax payment not from the date of the trial court's order.


OVERVIEW: The executor requested a refund of estate taxes after a profit-sharing trust was removed from the estate. The Department denied the request. Trial court granted the request but calculated the amount of interest from the date of its order. The executor sought review and contended that she was entitled to interest from the date the Department received her tax payment. The court found that the executor was not entitled to the refund because the assessment error was not discovered by the executor within the two year statute of limitations, as required by N.Y. Tax Law § 249-a(2). The court found that, because the executor, as the taxpayer, was seeking the refund, the six year statute of limitations was inapplicable. The court held that the differing time periods in the statute were not unconstitutional because the classification rationally furthered a legitimate state purpose. The court found additionally that the standard in matters of taxation was highly deferential. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the executor was not entitled to a refund of estate taxes assessed and collected by the Department.


HEADNOTES

Taxation - Tax Refund - Estate Taxes - Statute of Limitations A determination by the Department of Taxation and Finance which denied petitioner executor's application for a refund of estate taxes upon the sole ground that the Statute of Limitations had run should have been confirmed. In August 1988, petitioner voluntarily made a prepayment of an estimated estate tax, and the Department issued a refund on February 16, 1989 after Surrogate's Court fixed the estate tax, subsequent to which, by a supplemental order dated November 10, 1993, Surrogate's Court granted petitioner's request to reduce the value of the estate due to removal of a profit-sharing trust from the estate, and petitioner's request for a refund based on the supplemental order was denied. Because petitioner sought a refund based on a modified order, she was subject to the time limitations set forth in Tax Law former § 249-aa (1), which provides that if after payment of any tax pursuant to an order fixing such tax, such order is modified within two years, the executor is entitled to a refund if application is made within one year from the modification. Petitioner is not entitled to the six-year limitations period of Tax Law former § 249-aa (2), which provides that where a tax was paid before entry of a taxing order and such order shows that the amount of tax due is less than the amount paid, a refund is due if application sought within six years of entry of such taxing order. Tax Law former § 249-aa (2) is not applicable to applications for modifications or refunds related to such modifications. The second refund claim arises not out of a prepayment which was higher than the first order fixing the tax, but rather from a subsequent action that petitioner took to change the value of the estate. Therefore, Tax Law former § 249-aa (2), which speaks to an overpayment made because a prepayment exceeded the amount fixed by the first order, does not apply. Here, the taxpayer is seeking correction of the first order, and such a taxpayer is not in the same situation as one who claims a refund based on an original order, where only the ministerial act of filing for the refund is required.

Constitutional Law - Equal Protection of Laws - Estate Tax Refund - Statute of Limitations A determination by the Department of Taxation and Finance which denied petitioner executor's application for a refund of estate taxes upon the sole ground that the Statute of Limitations had run should have been confirmed. In August 1988, petitioner voluntarily made a prepayment of an estimated estate tax, and the Department issued a refund on February 16, 1989 after Surrogate's Court fixed the estate tax, subsequent to which, by a supplemental order dated November 10, 1993, Surrogate's Court granted petitioner's request to reduce the value of the estate due to removal of a profit-sharing trust from the estate, and petitioner's request for a refund based on the supplemental order was denied. Because petitioner sought a refund based on a modified order, she was subject to the time limitations set forth in Tax Law former § 249-aa (1), which provides that if after payment of any tax pursuant to an order fixing such tax, such order is modified within two years, the executor is entitled to a refund if application is made within one year from the modification. Petitioner is not entitled to the six-year limitations period of Tax Law former § 249-aa (2), which provides that where a tax was paid before entry of a taxing order and such order shows that the amount of tax due is less than the amount paid, a refund is due if sought within six years of entry of such taxing order. The differing time periods do not violate equal protection rights since rational policy reasons justify the different treatment accorded taxpayers under Tax Law former § 249-aa (1) and (2). Inasmuch as the two sections of the statute apply to two discrete categories of taxpayers--those who seek a refund based on an amended or corrected order and those who do not--the two groups are not identically situated. The longer time period under the second section is rationally related to a legitimate State interest in that it encourages taxpayers to make a timely estimated payment, and if that amount exceeds what is actually due, the taxpayer is given six years to seek a refund. This also encourages taxpayers to be diligent in establishing the worth of an estate because if the original order must be modified, the limitations period will be decreased. Requiring that a request for modification be made within two years furthers the interests of finality, especially if a taxpayer expects the modification to generate a refund.

 

309 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Tug Buster Bouchard Corp. v. Wetzler


71862


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


217 A.D.2d 192; 635 N.Y.S.2d 803; 1996 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 28



January 4, 1996, Decided  
January 4, 1996, Entered



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of the New York State Department of Taxation and Finance (state) appealed the order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which granted petitioner tug boats' application to the extent that it canceled the notices of deficiency issued by the state, declared N.Y. Tax Law § 301 facially discriminatory against interstate commerce, and awarded the tug boats costs.


OVERVIEW: The state conducted an audit of the tug boats for the period January 1984 through August 1990, at the conclusion of which the state issued an assessment in an aggregate amount including interest and penalties, pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law art. 13-A, commonly known as the Tax on Petroleum Businesses, N.Y. Tax Law § 300 et seq. The assessment was based upon a finding that, during the relevant period, the tug boats purchased fuel in New Jersey and thereafter imported and consumed such fuel in New York without paying the requisite "privilege" tax pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 301. The trial court granted the tug boats' application to the extent that it canceled the notices of deficiency, declared N.Y. Tax Law § 301 facially discriminatory against interstate commerce and awarded costs. The court modified the decision of the trial court. The tax did impermissibly burden the tug boats, and the tax violated the Commerce Clause. The court struck only N.Y. Tax Law § 301(a)(1)(ii), and not the whole Tax of Petroleum Businesses.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision of the trial court that cancelled the state's notice of tax deficiency for a petroleum use tax to the tug boats and struck only the offending part of New York's Tax on Petroleum Businesses.


HEADNOTES

Taxation - Petroleum Gross Receipts Tax - Commerce Clause In a proceeding brought by petitioners, corporations which provide barge and/or towing services using vessels powered by petroleum fuel purchased from out-of-State suppliers, seeking cancellation of notices of deficiency issued by the Department of Taxation and Finance based upon findings that petitioners had purchased fuel in New Jersey and thereafter imported and consumed such fuel in this State without paying the requisite "privilege" tax pursuant to Tax Law § 301, the notices of deficiency are cancelled and Tax Law § 301 (a) (1) (ii) is declared unconstitutional as facially discriminatory against interstate commerce. Respondent Commissioner of Taxation and Finance's argument that the tax imposed by Tax Law § 301 (a) (1) (ii) upon the purchasers and consumers of imported petroleum is also imposed upon the in-State purchasers and consumers of domestic petroleum because the sellers of domestic petroleum, who pay a use tax, "pass through" such tax to the in-State consumers in the form of higher prices, is premised upon the assumption, if not speculation, that the use tax paid by the in-State seller of domestic petroleum is equal to the tax imposed upon petitioners and those similarly situated, and such in-State seller will "pass along" the full amount of the use tax it paid to its customers, thereby negating the effect of, or offsetting, the burden imposed upon petitioners and those similarly situated by Tax Law § 301 (a) (1) (ii). Although the "pass through" theory has been recognized as a way of shifting tax expenses to in-State consumers by way of increased prices, unless respondent's assumptions are transformed into economic reality, in-State sellers of domestic petroleum remain benefited while petitioners and those similarly situated remain burdened, thereby leading to the conclusion that the tax at issue violates the Commerce Clause. Inasmuch as petitioners are not entitled to offset the sales tax paid in New Jersey or to any other out-of-State supplier against the tax imposed by Tax Law § 301 (a) (1) (ii), this provision results in multiple taxation and, as such, fails the internal consistency test, and results in impermissible interference with free trade.

Welcher v. Sobol


74062


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


222 A.D.2d 1001; 636 N.Y.S.2d 421; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13754



December 28, 1995, Decided  
December 28, 1995, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 30, 1996.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant principal sought review of an order of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which denied his motion for a preliminary injunction preventing respondent, New York State Commissioner of Education, from revoking his teaching credentials. After the commissioner revoked the principal's certifications under N.Y. Educ. Law § 305(7), the principal brought this action for a declaratory judgment that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Principal had permanent teaching certification and served as an elementary school principal. The commissioner issued a notice of substantial question as to moral character. Following an administrative hearing, the principal was found to have committed 25 incidents of sexual misconduct against his nieces, and his certificates were revoked. The principal argued that N.Y. Educ. Law § 305(7) was an unconstitutional delegation of power in that it failed to provide standards or guidance for the education commissioner. The court held that the statutory provision set forth an adequate standard and sufficient guidance to meet constitutional requirements, the principal did not demonstrate a likelihood of success on the merits, and the motion for a preliminary injunction was correctly denied. The court held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion because the principal's occupation involved contact with children, and because of his past conduct as found by the commissioner could be found to pose a threat to the health, safety, or welfare of children.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the lower court's denial of the motion for a preliminary injunction be affirmed.

Schulz v. Horseheads Cent. Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ.


73676


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


222 A.D.2d 819; 634 N.Y.S.2d 792; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12696



December 7, 1995, Decided  
December 7, 1995, Entered



DISPOSITION: ORDERED that the judgment is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, registered voters and taxpayers, appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Chemung County (New York), which granted respondent school district's motion to dismiss their petition seeking a declaratory judgment that the adoption of an austerity budget violated various provisions of the New York and United States Constitutions, and to declare N.Y. Educ. Law § 2023 and N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 209-a(1)(e) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The school district adopted an austerity budget for a particular school year and voted to levy the necessary taxes pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 2023 after two proposed budgets were rejected by the voters. The voters and taxpayers' action seeking declaratory judgment was dismissed by the trial court and they appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. The court held that N.Y. Const. art. II, § 1 was intended to regulate the qualifications of voters, not regulate the mode of elections. Accordingly the authorization for passage of an austerity budget, contained in N.Y. Educ. Law § 2023, did not abridge their right to a meaningful vote. The court also found no constitutional infirmity in the statute in that the challenged provisions were found to be reasonable in relation to their subject and adopted in the interests of the community. The court noted that the legislature had an obligation to provide and support public education and that § 2023 provided the mechanism to enforce that obligation. The court found all arguments raised by the taxpayers to lack merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayer and voters' petition which sought a declaratory judgment that the passage of an austerity budget by the school district was unconstitutional.

 

312 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Gazza v. New York State Dep't of Envtl. Conservation


94-00582


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


217 A.D.2d 202; 634 N.Y.S.2d 740; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12600


September 11, 1995, Argued  
December 4, 1995, Decided



DISPOSITION: ORDERED that the judgment is affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner brought a proceeding under N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 25-0404 to review respondent environmental conservation department's denial of a building permit. The Supreme Court in Suffolk County (New York) denied the petition and dismissed the proceeding, holding that the landowner could use the property for recreational purposes and that he was aware of its wetlands status when he purchased it. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner paid $ 100,000 cash for the property, $ 90,000 of which was used to discharge a federal tax lien. He testified that he was aware that most of the land had been inventoried as tidal wetlands. The court rejected the landowner's argument that the denial of the building permit diminished the value of his property from $ 396,000, its value as a buildable lot, to nothing, writing that the $ 100,000 purchase price reflected the environmental restrictions on the property. Thus, it held, it was unreasonable for the landowner to assume that he was purchasing the full unrestricted residential value of the property, and the trial court's conclusion that a "taking" did not occur upon the denial of the building permit should not be disturbed. It rejected the landowner's argument that the denial prevented him from using his property for any purpose, including recreational pursuits, stating that evidence indicated that local authorities would grant the permits necessary for the construction of a dock and catwalk on the parcel. Moreover, it noted, the landowner himself withdrew his variance application. Thus, it held, the economic value of the land had not been destroyed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law - Taking of Property - Tidal Wetlands - Building Permit Petitioner, who purchased property with the full knowledge that it had been designated protected tidal wetlands, cannot claim that a regulatory taking occurred when he was denied a building permit for a residence since he did not have a reasonable investment-backed expectation that he would be able to build a residence on his parcel. Petitioner asserts that until the building permit was denied by respondent there was always the possibility that he would be able to construct a residence on the parcel, and that it was not until that denial that he was made to suffer a regulatory taking which diminished the value of his property from $ 396,000 (its value as a buildable lot) to nothing. Petitioner's claim that, during his tenure of ownership, his property was worth $ 396,000 is belied by the $ 100,000 purchase price he paid for the property, a recent sale of a subject parcel generally being the "best evidence" of the parcel's value. Petitioner's argument that he will be unable to use his property for any purpose is without merit; there was evidence that local authorities would grant the appropriate variances and permits so as to allow the construction of a dock and catwalk on the parcel, and petitioner failed to meet his burden of proving that he would be unable to use his parcel for recreational purposes because the appropriate permits and variances would not be granted. Petitioner's withdrawal of his variance application prior to a decision of the Village Zoning Board is a probative fact militating against petitioner's claimed inability to utilize his property for any purpose. It cannot be said that Supreme Court erred when it determined that the economic value of the land had not been destroyed and that it retained significant value for recreational use. The amount petitioner paid for the property is strong proof of what his investment-backed expectations were at the time of the purchase. Petitioner, as a knowledgeable buyer, adjusted his purchase price to "offset" the restrictions that he knew had been placed on the property, and to give credence to petitioner's claim of a taking and grant his application for compensation would be to afford him a windfall that the law never intended taxpayers to shoulder.

Nils TT v. New York State Dep't of Soc. Servs.


73235


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


221 A.D.2d 874; 634 N.Y.S.2d 778; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12350



November 30, 1995, Decided  
November 30, 1995, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father brought a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to review a determination of respondent New York State Department of Social Services (department), which denied his request to have his name expunged from the New York State Central Register of Child Abuse and Maltreatment (register). The father alleged that N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 422(8) was unconstitutional in that its "some credible evidence" standard violated due process.


OVERVIEW: The register received several reports that the father had maltreated his two daughters. Subsequent investigations indicated against the father. He later requested that the reports be expunged from the register. After the register denied his request, the father sought a fair hearing pursuant to § 422(8). The department determined that some credible evidence existed to support the records and thus denied the expungement request. The father brought a Rule 78 proceeding for review of the determination, arguing that the "some credible evidence" standard violated due process. The court annulled the determination and remitted to the department. The court held that pursuant to its recent decision in another case, due process protection warranted replacement of the "some credible evidence" standard used in administrative expungement hearings with a higher "preponderance of the evidence" standard. Because the inclusion of the father's name on the register implicated a liberty interest protected by due process by placing a burden on his desired adoption prospects, the department's failure to use the higher standard was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the department's determination denying the father's request to expunge his name from the register, and remitted to the department for further proceedings.

People v. Padmore

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York) that convicted defendant of endangering the welfare of a child.

OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant of endangering the welfare of a child was affirmed because substantial evidence supported the jury's verdict and the child endangerment statute was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant.

The court concluded that any person of ordinary intelligence would understand that defendant's participation in a defrauding scheme for the benefit of an organized crime family was within the ambit of § 460.00 et seq.

Smith v. Board of Educ., Onteora Cent. Sch. Dist.


73282


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


221 A.D.2d 755; 633 N.Y.S.2d 625; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11156

November 9, 1995, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 18, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bus driver sought review of a determination of respondent school board, which terminated his employment for misconduct and insubordination in his attempt to discipline a student. The hearing officer had found the bus driver guilty only of picking up the student from his seat and recommended that he be suspended without pay up to a certain date, then reinstated.

The bus driver testified that he raised the student up and sat him back down in an effort to quiet him. The bus driver contended that N.Y. Civ. Serv. The findings of misconduct and insubordination were amply supported by the evidence adduced at the hearing. The resolution stated several grounds for the school board's determination and was read aloud at the meeting, which the bus driver attended. However, the school board did not give sufficient weight to mitigating factors warranting imposition of a lesser penalty. Those factors included the bus driver's above-average overall work performance evaluations and the student's consistent misbehavior problems both in the classroom and on the school bus.


OUTCOME: The court remitted the matter to the school board for imposition of an appropriate penalty for the bus driver's misconduct and insubordination.

319 of 992 DOCUMENTS


McCall v. State


74565


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


215 A.D.2d 1; 632 N.Y.S.2d 725; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10677



October 26, 1995, Decided  
October 26, 1995, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which, in two consolidated declaratory judgment actions, granted the motion for a preliminary injunction of plaintiffs, state comptroller and police conference president (officials), enjoining enforcement of Laws of 1995, ch. 119, § 16 and directing the state to begin paying pension supplements.


OVERVIEW: Ch. 119 increased the retirement benefits paid to certain former public employees. In addition, ch. 119, § 13 directed the officials to credit municipal employers with $ 230 million toward the payments required of them. The officials challenged the constitutionality of the credit mechanism, which they characterized as a "raid" on the pension fund, as well as ch. 119, § 16, which conditioned the commencement date of the benefit increase on the existence, and outcome, of any litigation challenging the credit provision. The officials contended that § 16 was an illegal attempt to insulate the law from any constitutional challenge or to "punish" the retirees for bringing such a challenge. The court held that the officials did not show that the denial of the request for an injunction would cause them to suffer any injury that was not compensable by money damages. Section 16 did not directly prevent the officials from bringing suit but merely required, as a condition of their exercise of the right to do so, that they forfeit certain monetary benefits. The officials could be compensated for the intervening delay by an order directing the payment of the allowances retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which directed the state to begin paying pension supplements and granted the officials' motions for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions - Preliminary Injunction - Increase in Public Employees' Retirement Benefits In two consolidated declaratory judgment actions challenging legislation which increases the retirement benefits paid to certain former public employees, and directs plaintiff Comptroller to credit the affected employees' employers with a total of $ 230 million toward the payments required of them, an order which granted plaintiffs' motions for a preliminary injunction enjoining enforcement of Laws of 1995 (ch 119, § 16) and directed defendant State of New York to begin paying pension supplements in September 1995 is reversed. Plaintiffs challenge the constitutionality of the credit mechanism (L 1995, ch 119, § 13), which they characterize as a "raid" on the pension fund, as well as that of section 16 of chapter 119, which conditions the commencement date of the benefit increase on the existence, and outcome, of any litigation challenging section 13. While plaintiffs contend that section 16 of chapter 119 improperly conditions the receipt of benefits upon the waiver of their constitutional right to petition the courts for redress and that such an impairment is all that need be shown to establish irreparable injury, even assuming that plaintiffs have established a likelihood that they will succeed in demonstrating that section 16 is constitutionally infirm, that fact is not sufficient to justify the issuance of a preliminary injunction, for section 16 does not directly prevent them from bringing suit, but merely requires, as a condition of their exercise of the right to do so, that they forfeit certain monetary benefits. As this loss can be fully redressed by a monetary award, should their challenge succeed, preliminary injunctive relief is not warranted. As for plaintiffs' argument that irreparable harm is manifest because it is highly probable that many of the retirees will die before receiving the supplemental allowances, if such an allegation were sufficient to demonstrate irremediable injury, that requirement would be satisfied in virtually every case, for any individual plaintiff bears the risk that he or she may expire before the matter is resolved. Absent extraordinary circumstances, not shown to be present here, a mere delay in payment of an additional benefit is not the kind of injury that warrants the awarding of equitable relief.

 

320 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Schulz v. New York State Bd. of Elections


74792


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


214 A.D.2d 224; 632 N.Y.S.2d 226; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10036



October 3, 1995, Decided  
October 3, 1995, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action pursuant to N.Y. Elec. Law § 16-104 and for declaratory judgment, petitioners sought review of an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which granted a motion by respondent State Board of Elections (New York) dismissing petitioners' fourth claim. The Board appealed an order of the same court granting petitioners' application to annul a proposition to amend N.Y. Const. art. VII, §§ 1, 2, 10, 11, 16.


OVERVIEW: New York's legislature sent a resolution to amend the state Constitution to the Board, which sent the proposal to the county election boards. Petitioners commenced an action challenging the proposal, alleging that the Board violated N.Y. Elec. Law § 4-108(2) by treating the proposed amendments as a single proposition, and that the form of submission failed to clearly and concisely state the proposition's purpose and effect. Petitioners also sought a declaration that N.Y. Elec. Law § 4-116 (amended 1993) unconstitutionally reduced the number of publishing newspapers to one per county. The trial court dismissed petitioners' latter claim and otherwise granted the petition. The Board appealed. On appeal, the court reversed and dismissed the petition. The court found that the proposed amendments' interrelationship required their submission as a single proposition, noting that separate submissions could have resulted in an ineffective or absurd result. The court rejected the contention that the proposition was ambiguous, noting that the Board had amply met the requirements of N.Y. Elec. Law § 4-108(1)(d) by presenting the proposition's purpose and effect in a clear and concise manner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the petition and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Elections - Constitutional Amendment - Publication Requirement In a combined proceeding and action challenging the wording of the text, abstract and form of a proposition to amend five sections of article VII of the NY Constitution with respect to the State's ability to contract certain debt, Supreme Court properly dismissed petitioners' claim that a 1993 amendment to Election Law § 4-116 (L 1993, ch 60, § 5), which reduced the publication period for propositions from two weeks to one week prior to election and which reduced the number of publishing newspapers from two per county to one per county, is unconstitutional. NY Constitution, article XIX, § 1, which provides that it shall be the duty of the Legislature to submit proposed amendments to the people for approval in such manner and at such times as the Legislature shall prescribe, clearly gives the Legislature the prerogative to designate the procedure to be used in submitting proposed amendments to the voters. The Legislature was acting within this authority in amending the publication requirements contained in Election Law § 4-116.

Elections - Constitutional Amendment - Form of Proposition Supreme Court erred in declaring the text, abstract and form of a proposition to amend five sections of article VII of the NY Constitution with respect to the State's ability to contract certain debt to be null and void. When, as here, a proposed constitutional amendment is to be submitted to the voters in a general election, the State Board of Elections is to transmit to each County Board of Elections a certified copy of the text of each amendment, proposition or question and a statement of the form in which it is to be submitted, and if more than one such amendment, proposition or question is to be voted upon, each such amendment, proposition or question shall be separately and consecutively numbered (Election Law § 4-108). While petitioners contend that because five sections of NY Constitution article VII were proposed to be amended the State Board was required to set forth five separate and consecutively numbered corresponding propositions, Election Law § 4-108 speaks in terms of the proposed "amendment, proposition or question" to be submitted to the voters, and viewed as a whole, implicitly acknowledges that numerous proposed amendments may be presented as a single "proposition" or "question". Further, the proposed amendments herein are contextually interrelated to such a degree that they must stand or fall together to have any effect. The submission of five separate propositions could theoretically result in the approval of some, but not all, of the interrelated proposed amendments, and the approval of three of the amendments, which contain cross references to the two other proposed additions would have an absurd result if the latter additions were not approved; they would cross reference nonexistent provisions.

Elections - Constitutional Amendment - Form of Abstract In a combined proceeding and action challenging the wording of the text, abstract and form of a proposition to amend five sections of article VII of the NY Constitution with respect to the State's ability to contract certain debt, there is no merit to petitioners' claims that the abstract certified by the State Board of Elections fails to concisely state the purpose and effect of the proposed amendments in "a clear and coherent manner using words with common and everyday meanings" as required by Election Law § 4-108 (1) (d), and that the form of submission certified by the State Board fails to indicate the subject matter of the proposed amendments "in a clear and coherent manner" as required by Election Law § 4-108 (2). The abstract clearly and coherently conveys the purpose and effect of the proposition; the first line states that the purpose of the proposal is to revise the State's borrowing practices, and balance of the abstract briefly outlines, in understandable language, the proposed changes and the effect of those changes. Similarly, the form of submission has an abbreviated title which clearly and coherently indicates the subject matter of the proposal. While the State Board arguably could have worded the form of submission in a number of different ways, the paragraph which describes the proposal concisely and accurately sets forth, in understandable terms, a brief summary of that which is set forth in the text and abstract.

Building Contractors Ass'n v. State


93-06372


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


218 A.D.2d 722; 630 N.Y.S.2d 763; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8833


March 13, 1995, Argued  
August 21, 1995, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff building contractor associations, labor unions, and local government associations appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York) that rejected their constitutional challenge to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 101.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff building contractor associations, labor unions, and local government associations appealed a judgment favoring defendant state government and intervenor electrical contractors association in plaintiffs' lawsuit seeking to declare a state statute constitutional. Plaintiffs had sought to strike down the state law requiring specific specifications and bidding for certain types of work performed in the construction of public projects. The court affirmed, thereby upholding the statute. It held that plaintiffs had failed to prove that the purpose of the statute was to favor certain interests in the construction industry. Instead, what was established was that the law was one that ultimately favored the taxpayers, and thus there was a valid state interest in regulating public works contracts. In addition, the statute was a general law, not a special law.


OUTCOME: The judgment below was affirmed. The statute in question was constitutional, as it was a general law and was one that favored the taxpayers.

Burke v. Denison


72917


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


218 A.D.2d 894; 630 N.Y.S.2d 421; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8660



August 10, 1995, Decided  
August 10, 1995, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner purchaser appealed a decision from the Supreme Court of Albany County (New York), which dismissed his application in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding and filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment to review a decision by respondent Zoning Board of Appeals of the City of Albany (board) denying his request for a special use permit. The purchaser claimed the board's decision was arbitrary, capricious, and without a rational basis.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser was interested in buying certain real property within the city and applied to the board for a special use permit in order that he might construct a take-out/carry-out restaurant comprised of three separate food franchises with a common eating area. The board denied the application, but the ruling was thereafter annulled by the trial court. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and, noting that the provisions of the zoning ordinance regarding parking had been amended, remitted the matter to the board, where it was again denied. The board found that the proposed use constituted a "take-out, carry-out restaurant" and that the number of off-street parking spaces proposed violated the requirements of the zoning ordinance. The purchaser sought a declaratory judgment action seeking to annul the board's determination and have the provision of the zoning ordinance defining "take-out, carry-out restaurant" declared void for vagueness. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the board's decision was amply supported by the evidence, and that the purchaser failed to establish any constitutional deficiency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the board denying the purchaser's application for a special use permit to open a take-out, carry-out restaurant within the city.

 

324 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. Park Madison Prof'l Lab.


94-01225


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


212 A.D.2d 271; 630 N.Y.S.2d 37; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2216


February 8, 1995, Submitted  
July 20, 1995, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physician sought review of the judgment from the supreme court (New York), which denied his motion for summary judgment against plaintiff patient in the patient's action for medical malpractice occurring during an abortion procedure.


OVERVIEW: The patient consulted a gynecologist about options for terminating her pregnancy and signed a consent form which she acknowledged, during her deposition testimony, that she had read and fully understood. After the procedure the patient suffered extensive bleeding and was treated for a perforation of her uterus. The patient charged the physician with malpractice in failing to obtain plaintiff's informed consent before the procedure was undertaken. In asserting the cause of action for lack of informed consent, plaintiff argued that she was not a proper candidate for the procedure, that it violated her religious beliefs, and that she should have been talked out of it. The physician moved for summary judgment, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court. The court held that the evidence in this case showed that the patient was specifically told of the risk of sadness and depression and the possibility of serious depression as a result of an abortion. The court found that summary judgment was warranted because there was no question of fact that the patient was informed of these risks.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the physician's motion for summary judgment in the patient's medical malpractice action.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and Surgeons - Lack of Informed Consent In a medical malpractice action, defendant doctor's motion to dismiss plaintiff's cause of action for lack of informed consent should have been granted. Plaintiff, who suffered extensive bleeding and was treated for a perforation of her uterus following a second trimester abortion performed by defendants, was specifically told that once dilators were inserted into her cervix she was committed to completing the procedure, and when she returned the following day, defendant doctor, without further discussion with plaintiff, completed the procedure. Plaintiff had been advised of the possible risks of hemorrhage and perforation, and was specifically told of the risk of sadness and depression and the possibility of serious depression as a result of an abortion. There can be no claim that plaintiff was persuaded to have an abortion that was, without her knowledge, "needless" according to her own convictions; she cannot seek to hold defendant liable because her personal convictions have apparently changed since she consented to and underwent the procedure. While plaintiff argues that an attempt should have been made to talk her out of the abortion and that because she was in a "crisis pregnancy" she should have been referred to several days of independent counseling, these are not permissible requirements. Plaintiff was thoroughly advised of the risks and alternatives to her abortion and she gave her informed consent to the procedure; there is no merit to the contention that defendant, who first saw plaintiff on the day after the dilators had initially been inserted was negligent because he did not advise her again of all the risks, both physical and emotional, and did not seek at that point to dissuade her from completing the abortion procedure which it is claimed may not have been irreversible. The extensive information and counseling given to plaintiff by the clinic personnel provided her with all the necessary information to enable her to make the requisite knowledgeable decision and defendant's reliance thereon fulfilled his obligations in that regard.

Estate of Smith v. Atlas Assembly/Crawford Furniture Mfg. Corp.


71285


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


216 A.D.2d 804; 628 N.Y.S.2d 872; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7457



June 29, 1995, Decided  
June 29, 1995, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and the employer's workers' compensation insurance carrier (insurance carrier) sought review of a decision of respondent Workers' Compensation Board (board), which affirmed a workers' compensation law judge's determination that the employer and the insurance carrier were to pay certain death benefits under N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 16(4)(b) to the mother of an employee who was killed in the course of his employment.


OVERVIEW: After the employee was killed in an industrial accident in the course of his employment, the board affirmed a decision by a workers' compensation law judge directing the employer and the insurance carrier to pay certain death benefits to the employee's mother pursuant to § 16(4)(b) and to pay a certain amount to the Uninsured Employers Fund and the Vocational Rehabilitation Fund. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 16(4)(b) was constitutionally valid. Noting that the purpose of the Workers' Compensation Law was not only the protection of the employee and the employee's dependents, but also the protection of the employer from further lawsuits, the court held that § 16(4)(b) was consistent with N.Y. Const. art. I, § 18, which created a broad mandate authorizing the legislature to allow for death benefits to nondependent parents or a decedent's estate. The court held that neither the employer or the insurance carrier had standing to assert a violation of the equal protection rights of dependent surviving parents or surviving spouses and that § 16(4)(b) did not violate the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of either the state or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decision that affirmed a workers' compensation law judge's determination that the employer and the insurance carrier were to pay certain death benefits to the mother of an employee who was killed in the course of his employment.

Castle Oil Corp. v. City of New York


55123


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


216 A.D.2d 60; 627 N.Y.S.2d 650; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6097



June 8, 1995, Decided  
June 8, 1995, ENTERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment by the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which declared that New York City, N.Y. Admin. Code § 11-602(8)(b)(3) (1986), also known as Local Law No. 3, unconstitutional, insofar as it prohibited deduction of petroleum taxes imposed pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 301 in determining the general corporation tax liability.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted art. 13-A of the Tax Law, N.Y. Tax Law § 301, which imposed a petroleum tax on oil companies, and amended art. 9-A of the Tax Law, N.Y. Tax Law § 208(9)(b)(4), to disallow the deductibility of the petroleum tax from the corporate taxpayer's income. The New York City Council enacted Local Law No. 3 to conform the city tax law. The state legislature then amended both articles by deleting the disallowance of petroleum tax for purposes of the franchise tax, but the city did not amend the administrative code. The oil companies brought an action alleging that the city had to amend the local law to comport with the state law. The trial court declared Local Law No. 3 unconstitutional, and on appeal the court affirmed, holding that the local law imposing taxes on general corporations should substantially follow the model local law contained in the enabling act, 1966 N.Y. Laws ch. 772, § 1, or it may depart from the model local law to impose a tax that conformed with art. 9-A. The court determined that the local law was intrinsically subordinate to and had to comport with any specifically reference state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that held the Local Law No. 3 was unconstitutional.

New York State Crime Victims Bd. v. Abbott


53914, 53915


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


212 A.D.2d 22; 627 N.Y.S.2d 629; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5875



June 1, 1995, Decided  
June 1, 1995, ENTERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of an order and judgment of the Supreme Court (New York), which referred to a special referee all claims relevant to funds held by respondent New York State Crime Victims Board, pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law § 632-a, and which dismissed appellant's third-party complaint as abandoned. Respondent had commenced the underlying interpleader action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 1006(f).


OVERVIEW: Respondent New York State Crime Victims Board collected funds pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law § 632-a. After that law was declared unconstitutional, respondent commenced an interpleader action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 1006(f) seeking to gain judicial disposition of the various funds among a broad group of competing claimants, which included victims, judgment creditors, and the criminals themselves. Appellant claimant initiated a third-party action against third-party respondent publishing company. The trial court referred all of the claims to a special referee to hear and report on the accounts. The court also granted the motion to dismiss appellant's third-party complaint as abandoned. On appeal, the court affirmed the referral and the dismissal of appellant's third-party complaint. Appellant's third-party complaint was properly dismissed on the merits because three of appellant's causes of action were raised and rejected on the merits in prior, related litigation. The fourth cause of action was devoid of merit. Respondent could not be held liable for enforcing a statute that later was found to be unconstitutional because its unconstitutionality was not plain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and judgment. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in referring the matter to a special referee. Appellant claimant's third-party complaint was properly dismissed because he defaulted on the motion to dismiss and failed to offered any explanation for the default, and because three of his causes of action had been rejected on the merits in prior, related litigation and the fourth was without merit.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - Crime Victims Board - Disposition of Funds Following Invalidation of "Son of Sam" Law - Reference to Special Referee In an interpleader action (CPLR 1006 [f]) commenced by plaintiff New York State Crime Victims Board to obtain judicial disposition of the various "profits" from crime being held in special escrow accounts pursuant to the "Son of Sam" law (Executive Law § 632-a) following the statute's invalidation by the United States Supreme Court as being violative of the First Amendment right of free speech, the IAS Court properly referred all of the claims of the competing claimants to a Special Referee to hear and report on the accounts and properly rejected the argument of appellant prison inmate, a claimant to the funds held with respect to a fellow inmate regarding royalties from the 1975 film Dog Day Afternoon, that the Board was obligated, once the statute was declared unconstitutional, to return the money to the various sources from which it originated. To direct the Board to return the money to the different sources would not serve a legitimate purpose and would engender a situation fertile for the filing of numerous, additional lawsuits. Moreover, since all of the necessary parties with claims to the funds are within the court's jurisdiction and since the IAS Court is the proper forum in which to resolve the competing claims, it was not an abuse of discretion to deny appellant's request to direct the return of the money to the payors. Furthermore, an appellate court will not ordinarily interfere with the discretion of the trial courts in referring a matter to a Special Referee to hear and report, especially where, as here, no substantial right of any party is affected.

Crimes - Crime Victims Board - Disposition of Funds Following Invalidation of "Son of Sam" Law - No Liability for Enforcement of Unconstitutional Statute In an interpleader action (CPLR 1006 [f]) commenced by plaintiff New York State Crime Victims Board to obtain judicial disposition of the various "profits" from crime being held in special escrow accounts pursuant to the "Son of Sam" law (Executive Law § 632-a) following the statute's invalidation by the United States Supreme Court as being violative of the First Amendment right of free speech, the IAS Court properly referred all of the claims of the competing claimants to a Special Referee to hear and report on the accounts and was not required to address the counterclaims asserted by appellant prison inmate, a claimant to the funds held with respect to a fellow inmate regarding royalties from the 1975 film Dog Day Afternoon, seeking indemnification from the Board on the theory that it knew or should have known that the "Son of Sam" law was unconstitutional. Since the statute, prior to its invalidation, was continually upheld by various State and Federal Courts, the Board cannot be held liable for enforcing a statute that was later found to be unconstitutional where that unconstitutionality was not plain.

Crimes - Crime Victims Board - Disposition of Funds Following Invalidation of "Son of Sam" Law - Res Judicata In an interpleader action (CPLR 1006 [f]) commenced by plaintiff New York State Crime Victims Board to obtain judicial disposition of the various "profits" from crime being held in special escrow accounts pursuant to the "Son of Sam" law (Executive Law § 632-a) following the statute's invalidation by the United States Supreme Court as being violative of the First Amendment right of free speech, the IAS Court properly dismissed the third-party action in which appellant inmate sought funds held with respect to a fellow inmate regarding royalties from the movie Dog Day Afternoon, since, in addition to appellant's inexcusable default on the motion to dismiss, the first three causes of action were raised and rejected on the merits in prior, related litigation and are thus barred by res judicata, and the fourth cause of action against the Board lacks merit. Lastly, appellant's contention that the IAS Court's decision to impose a $ 200 sanction upon him was improper also lacks merit since the $ 200, rather than a sanction, is merely a normal assessment of costs.

Pet Professionals v. City of New York


93-04134


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


215 A.D.2d 742; 627 N.Y.S.2d 728; 1995 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5772


April 28, 1995, Submitted  
May 30, 1995, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to declare 24 R.C.N.Y. §§ 161.04 and 161.15 unconstitutional, plaintiff agency sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which denied the agency's motion to strike defendant city's answer, denied the agency's motion for summary judgment, and granted the city's cross-motion for summary judgment dismissing the agency's complaint.


OVERVIEW: The board of health adopted 24 R.C.N.Y. §§ 161.04 and 161.15, implementing a new dog licensing program, which provided that those who issued a permit pursuant to 24 R.C.N.Y. § 161.09 were required to provide a dog license application to any individual seeking to purchase, adopt, groom, train, or board a dog. In addition, the permittees were required to report on a monthly basis all licensed or unlicensed dogs that had been sold, adopted, groomed, trained, boarded, sheltered, or otherwise served. The agency filed an action to determine the constitutionality of 24 R.C.N.Y. §§ 161.04 and 161.15. Further, the court held that the agency failed to establish that the amendments were so lacking in reason for their promulgation because controlling animals within the city was a legitimate governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting the city's motion for summary judgment was modified by adding a provision declaring that 24 R.C.N.Y. §§ 161.04 and 161.15 were constitutional; otherwise the judgment was affirmed.
